### Post by ilikenwf on 2007-11-26
[CENTER][SIZE="5"]Zen Kernel[/SIZE]

Caveats: [See the wiki to get the nVidia drivers to work!]("https://wiki.ubuntu.com/ZenKernel")

[CENTER][SIZE="5"]NOW ANNOUNCING buildZen version 2!
This script should now be compatible with any distro, although it currently is easiest on Debian based distros[/SIZE][/CENTER]

buildZen is a bash script that guides you through the process of building the Zen kernel yourself. It makes it very, very easy! Just follow the prompts as you go along! It is not one time use, as you can run it again, when you are ready to update your source tree and build the kernel again. Just follow the instructions in the prompts, and you will be fine!

This is a beta, but it works. Please tell me of any issues you encounter. You can either download it by clicking [here]("http://www.mattparnell.com/zen/prefab/buildZen"), or you can copy and paste from below. Put it in a text file named buildZen, and chmod +x buildZen after that. Then, to run the script, use sudo sh buildZen and follow the directions. Note that xconfig or gconfig should be used first, as they are easier to use when you get to the configuration step. Note that if you exit the script, you can always leave off from where you left off. Hopefully, this script will be a crutch to teach you how to configure and compile, and you will eventually stop using it and doing it the normal way.

Good luck, and have fun! Make sure to leave one default Ubuntu kernel installed at all times, as a fallback! Don't forget the wiki article, as it will contain information regarding not only buildZen, but other topics, such as firmware for wireless drivers, and nVidia and ATI installation directions.

Fixes: permissions should now be automatically set, and if root isn't running the script, it exits. Furthermore, everything should go nicely.

**READ THE DOCUMENTATION [ON THE WIKI!]("https://wiki.ubuntu.com/ZenKernel")**

**[AND SEE THE OFFICIAL ZEN SITE!]("http://zen-sources.org")**

**[COLOR="Red"]ALWAYS KEEP ANOTHER KERNEL INSTALLED TO FALL BACK ON IN THE EVENT THIS ONE MAY FAIL![/COLOR]**

Now updated, **buildZen v2** should work with pretty much any distro, now. It's easiest still with debian based distros, as for all others it checks to see if an automatic build system is in place like portage or abs, and if not, it uses the old fashioned make clean, make, make install, etc...I need people to help me put more checks in for any other build systems to make this really compatible with everything else...oh yeah...and I'll add color again eventually.

```
#!/bin/sh

#This script is opensource under the GPL. Please attribute it and any part of it you use to Matt Parnell, and #http://www.mattparnell.com/zen/. To use, chmod +x the script, and then run it by either dropping it into your #/sbin/ dir, or ./buildZen to run it. It pretty well explains everything it's doing. To contact me, or give me #commentary or improvements, see http://www.mattparnell.com/, or email me at admin@mattparnell.com. 

echo -en "
[INTRODUCTION]
This script will aid you in building the Zen kernel, which you will be building from the git tree. Rerun this script whenever you want to rebuild or update the source tree. 

To continue, type zen to install the regular Zen kernel, zenrt to install the Zen realtime kernel, zenmm to install the Zenmm kernel, or zenps3 to build the Zen for Playstation 3 kernel. Otherwise, enter nothing to exit. Any other input will result in an error. 

";


read repo;

if [ "x${repo}" == "x" ]; then
exit;
fi

echo "[CHECKING FOR BUILD DEPENDENCIES]";

if [[ $(uname -a |grep buntu) != "" || $(uname -a |grep debian) != "" || $(uname -a |grep mint) != "" ]]; then
echo "Installing dependencies";
apt-get update;
apt-get -y install kernel-package libncurses5-dev git bzip2 wget;
fi

if [[ $(which git) == "" ||$(which gcc) == "" || $(which make) == "" || $(which autoconf) == "" || $(which automake) == "" ]]; then 
echo "It appears you do not have gcc, make, autoconf, or automake installed. Please install and rerun this script.";
exit;
fi

echo "It appears you have all build dependencies.


[CLONE THE SOURCE TREE]
Now, we must clone the sources via git, using the command \"git clone\". The cloning process takes anywhere from 5 to 60 minutes, sometimes more. Go grab a coffee or surf the web. It's worth the wait. May I suggest browsing mattparnell.com ?

";

cd /usr/src/;

if [ -d /usr/src/"$repo" ]; then

echo "We just need to update your current source. If any errors happen, and you can't fix them, delete the source folder and try again.";

cd /usr/src/"$repo";
git pull;

echo "Everthing's up to date, or git has timed out.";

else
echo "Cloning "$repo"...";

git clone http://git.zen-sources.org/kernel/"$repo".git;

echo "

The source is now cloned on your local drive."

fi

echo "[CHANGING CONFIGURATION OPTIONS]
From here the options are all up to your discretion. It is suggested that you deselect any drivers, functions, or other options that you know you will not use. If in doubt, disable it. If something is broken or the kernel does not boot, just remove it, re-enable the option, and build. Make sure to take notes your first few tries, and remember to uninstall your old and broken Zen kernels. Always leave a default kernel installed to fall back on! Note that your configuration will be backed up to your home directory.


To configure your kernel, we need to know what interface you wish to use. 

xconfig:    1 (Requires qt)
gconfig:    2 (Requires gtk)
menuconfig: 3 (Requires ncurses)
oldconfig:  4 (Requires bash)

When finished, save and close the interface you choose to continue on to the building process.

Choice: "

read I;
cd /usr/src/"$repo"/;

if [ "$I" = "1" ]; then
make xconfig;
elif [ "$I" = "2" ]; then
make gconfig;
elif [ "$I" = "3" ]; then
make menuconfig;
else
make oldconfig;
fi

cp .config ~/kernel.config;

echo "

[BUILD THE KERNEL]
Now that that is all over, we are finally ready to build your kernel. Ubuntu has a script that automates the process, in which it builds your kernel into a nice deb package. You can install that, I hope. All that is left is issuing the command to make that package. This will take some time, and will take all of your computing resources. This is a really good time to walk off for 30 minutes to an hour, and do something else. 

To continue, enter y. Otherwise, enter n to exit:

";

read BD;
cd /usr/src/"$repo"/;

if [ "$BD" == "n" ]; then
exit;
fi

if [ $(which make-kpkg) != "" ]; then
INSTALL_MOD_STRIP=1 CONCURRENCY_LEVEL=2 make-kpkg --initrd kernel_image kernel_headers modules_image;

echo "Done building, you should have a kernel and headers package to install in /usr/src, as well as a modules package if you opted to put any module source in /usr/src."

elif [ $(which makepkg) != "" ]; then
echo "D'oh. Don't you know there's a PKGBUILD in AUR for this? Go get it, and make sure to move your kernel source tree to the PKGBUILD's appropriate src directory. You may have to edit the git url, as it has changed, and the maintainer is a bit late on updating such things."

else
echo "Doing it the old fashioned way";
make clean;
make;
make bzImage;
make modules;
make modules_install;
fi

echo "Building done. You now need to follow your distro's specific procedures to create a cpio/initrd image, and edit your lilo.conf or /boot/grub/menu.lst file appropriately. See your respective wiki to figure this one out.


[SUPPORT]
Read the Zen Kernel entry in the Ubuntu wiki to learn how to install wireless firmware, and setup the TuxOnIce suspend features, among others. To install the nVidia drivers, you will need the nVidia installer, as well as a patch available at http://www.mattparnell.com/zen/PKGBUILD/nvidia/xen.patch.txt if it doesn't work.

For live support, feel free to use IRC to connect to irc://irc.freenode.net and join the #zen-sources channel.

You may want to see zen-sources.org, as well as the Zen thread on the Gentoo forums, which is linked to at mattparnell.com/zen.html. You can find further support in the Zen thread on Ubuntuforums.";

exit;
```

[/CENTER]

### Post by drdabbles on 2007-11-27
Cross compiling is, to put it lightly, a real pain. It's not impossible, and for a great example of how to do it, I would suggest you take a peek at the Buildroot project linked to from the uClibc webpages.

Having said that, are you including any of the nVidia graphics drivers, or are you leaving it to the user to manually install those whenever they upgrade to your latest build?

### Post by reclusivemonkey on 2007-11-27
Damn I wish this had appeared a couple of days ago. I just downgraded to Feisty on my laptop as I was sick of not having a working kernel for my laptop on Gutsy. Will this work on Feisty?

---

### Post by ilikenwf on 2007-11-27
This should work with Feisty, and no, the nvidia and ATI drivers aren't included. To use them, edit your /etc/X11/xorg.conf and find the section that mentions using the "nvidia" (or ATI) driver. change it to nv or vesa, save, restart X, and then install and run Envy ( [http://www.albertomilone.com/nvidia_scripts1.html](http://www.albertomilone.com/nvidia_scripts1.html) ) Then either allow Envy to (I suggest doing it yourself) or change yourself the X11 file back to the way it was...Envy is nice because it does all of the dirty work.

Note: The kernel image itself is 1.6mb

---

### Post by Waninkoko on 2007-11-27
Try this:

ln -s /usr/src/linux-headers-2.6.24-rc3-zen3-ubuntu-x64/include/asm-x86 /usr/src/linux-headers-2.6.24-rc3-zen3-ubuntu-x64/asm

About truecrypt, it doesn't work because of ABI changes.

### Post by jaffa_nz on 2007-12-02
Kia Ora.

Partial newbie - sort of a "longterm trouble with this and that fighter till i give up or downgrade"..  quick couple of questions.

With all of the kernel freezes and the like with Ubuntu Gutsy, i was wanting to get onto a kernel more forward than  [2.6.22-14-generic #1 SMP] i have intel video and broadcom wireless (working with restricted drivers)  in a Dell d620 Laptop.  
Will my wireless etc work if i install your kernel or do i need to use Ndis again.  
Will the installation leave me with the previous kernel above on the grub menu to revert to?
Will compiz-fusion work.

appreciate your responses, have a great week.

---

### Post by ilikenwf on 2007-12-02
1. It will work, but with ndiswrapper. The best way to go about this is using the newest version. I have a broadcom card, and I get full speed. Unless you are hacking wifi networks, ndiswrapper is better despite the hassle as you get the full 54mbps instead of being limited to 11 with the restricted driver.

2. Yes, you will have your previous kernel until you manually uninstall it and it's headers. It is always good to keep your last old kernel to revert to.

3. Is your video card using a restricted driver? If not, it has the kernel mode drivers built in, and compiz will work out of the box. Otherwise, you can d/l and install intel's driver.

That said, you should wait until the next release, as this one is quite buggy.

---

### Post by anansesem on 2007-12-03
This kernel does not want to detect my SATA drives.  I get an ALERT error stating that it could not find the boot drive then I'm thrown into BusyBox shell.  The drive is specified by UUID in GRUB menu.  I am able to boot with the same configurations with a straight 2.6.24-rc3 kernel.  Anyone else getting this?

### Post by hardran3 on 2007-12-03
I got my ipw2100 wireless working by doing this

```
sudo ln -s /lib/firmware/2.6.22-14-generic /lib/firmware/2.6.24-rc3-zen3-ubuntu-x86
```

---

As for this:
I got my ipw2100 wireless working by doing this

Code:

sudo ln -s /lib/firmware/2.6.22-14-generic /lib/firmware/2.6.24-rc3-zen3-ubuntu-x86

That is a good idea...that is a little hack you can do to get quite a bit working. For the person earlier in this thread who used broadcom drivers, you could try doing this. I believe Envy takes a similar approach.

I'm on  x86.

### Post by ilikenwf on 2007-12-04

### Post by ilikenwf on 2007-12-04
> **adrianmak said:**
> should i just download the .deb , double-click to install, that's all.

You download the .deb for the image and the headers. You can install them by clicking them, but it would be faster to open a terminal, go to the place you downloaded the debs to, and type "sudo dpkg -i *.deb" and wait. When done, reboot and give it a try...you may have to use ndiswrapper if your wireless isn't supported, and please take note that it is a good idea to change the driver in /etc/X11/xorg.conf to a generic one if you use a proprietary or restricted driver for video...vesa is good generically until you can install your video driver, otherwise, use envy for nvidia and ati...

Just reiterating myself there...

> **xArv3nx said:**
> How good is the speed increase?

I tried the CK sources and they greatly increased my speed in games and Cedega.

How will this fare against CK patches?

This kernel has the CK patches, modified to work with this source, and to work with the CFS scheduler. It varies from machine to machine, but the increase should be noticeable on all machines. The CFS scheduler, alongside many other patches and tweaks, not to mention better code (2.6.24) makes it really fast for me. Power consumption is also cut down, with the addition of more drivers, too. Your Cedega modules may or may not compile at this point, because most devs are focused on 2.6.23 right now...

---

Try this:
```
sudo ln -s /lib/firmware/(ubuntu's generic kernel here without the parenthases) /lib/firmware/(whatever version you are using...copy  the name of my kernel you are using and put it here without the parentheses)
```

Then:

```
sudo dpkg--reconfigure linux-image-2.6.24(hit tab)
```
```
hit enter
```

Then, reboot.

sudo dpkg --remove linux-headers-2.6.24 (hit tab here)

### Post by anansesem on 2007-12-05
Have installed the rc4-zen0 source and works nicely.  

I had Nvida drivers installed with a previous kernel but simply running the .run package did not install.  So I did the following to get it installed:

SYSSRC=/usr/src/linux nvidia-installer -f.

The "-f" forces update of the driver (You need internet connection for it to download lates driver from nvidia site.

Thanks for this.

### Post by zenrox on 2007-12-06

---

### Post by ilikenwf on 2007-12-06
> **zenrox said:**
> i have bine tryin to get it to compile for the last 3 day
why dont you post a down and dirty howto for your kernel the way you do it

**_Down and Dirty:_**

1.Get the source, drop it into /usr/src/ and extract

2. ```
sudo make xconfig
``` (while in /usr/src/zen-sources)

3.Configure options as you would like OR just use this config file:
[http://www.mattparnell.com/zen/2.6.24-rc4-zen0/config/x86_64std](http://www.mattparnell.com/zen/2.6.24-rc4-zen0/config/x86_64std)

4.Please note I haven't perfected my x86 config file yet, but I will, and then upload it. There are extra x86 options you will have to configure.

5. Then, to compile, issue the following all in one line:
```
INSTALL_MOD_STRIP=1 CONCURRENCY_LEVEL=4 CC="gcc-4.1 -Os -funit-at-a-time -mregparm=3" sudo make-kpkg --initrd kernel_image kernel_headers --append-to-version=-yourversionhere
```

6. The debs will be dumped into /usr/src when everything is done compiling. To install, just do this:
```
sudo dpkg -i *.deb
```

---

### Post by bornagainpenguin on 2007-12-08
I managed to get the new kernel to install on Feisty, but I had to do a little running to grab dependencies in order to do it... LOL I felt like I was back on an RPM distro for a bit there...

These are the files I needed to make the kernel headers install:

```
gcc-4.2-base_4.2.1-5ubuntu4_i386.deb
libc6_2.6.1-1ubuntu9_i386.deb
libgcc1_4.2.1-5ubuntu4_i386.deb
libstdc++6_4.2.1-5ubuntu4_i386.deb
zlib1g_1.2.3.3.dfsg-5ubuntu2_i386.deb
```
You can find them all here: [http://packages.ubuntu.com](http://packages.ubuntu.com)

The one area I'm still having difficulty is Tux on Ice.  I've edited the menu.lst file as according to the instructions but it's just refusing to hibernate.  I'll try messing with that later.

For now I'm happy with the new kerenel on my Feisty.  It seems to boot faster--it certainly boots smoother, less jerks on the splash screen progress bar.  I like it!

Thanks again for porting this over and compiling it for us!

--bornagainpenguin (hoping the dependencies list posted above will help others)

PS: I used the Gusty editions of all files listed above and simply clicked through the warnings.  Seems to have not hurt anything but time will tell....

### Post by Muty-bg on 2007-12-08
ok this look familiar :)

I think it's related to this:
> 

>Hi
>commit to .24 tree:
>[http://git.kernel.org/?p=linux/kernel/git/torvalds/linux-2.6.git;a=co](http://git.kernel.org/?p=linux/kernel/git/torvalds/linux-2.6.git;a=co)...

>introduces:
>+EXPORT_SYMBOL_GPL(pv_mmu_ops);
>+EXPORT_SYMBOL_GPL(pv_cpu_ops);

>pv_cpu_ops is for nvidia
>pv_mmu_ops' is for amd(ati)

Speaking of which, the patch introduced a strict-aliasing warning (that
is, common userspace program compilation would warn about such) at:

+       return *((void **)&tmpl + type);

&tmpl is of type struct paravirt_patch_template **, and cross-casting
this to void ** usually gives a strict-aliasing warning.
A workaround is to pre-cast to void *,
        return *((void **)(void *)&tmpl + type);
is that ok? 


Here's a link to the original post: [http://groups.google.com/group/linux.kernel/browse_thread/thread/2d57b8dd99fe2b2a](http://groups.google.com/group/linux.kernel/browse_thread/thread/2d57b8dd99fe2b2a)

---

### Post by Muty-bg on 2007-12-08
OK so I found the culprit for the problem and a patch for it. I'll try to patch the kernel and recompile it.Hope it works.

Keep in mind that this problem only affects the 32bit version

### Post by ilikenwf on 2007-12-08
Waninkoko has informed me these problems are because paravirtualization support is enabled in the kernel configs. From now on (until the kernel.org devs get it fixed we will have to disable this feature, as it is a vanilla kernel issue). 

So, if you are compiling, disable paravirtualization support. I will try to get an updated 64 bit version out soon.

---

### Post by Waninkoko on 2007-12-08
Paravirtualization is used rarely so disable it is the safest way.

Btw, ilikenwf, enable IWL3945 and IWL4965 drivers. They work really well but users need to download the ucode (firmware) from [http://intellinuxwireless.org](http://intellinuxwireless.org)

---

### Post by ilikenwf on 2007-12-10
I need you guys to answer the following questions via PM to me (ilikenwf):

1. What architecture do you use?
   x86
   x86_64
   AMD64
   other (specify)

2.How many cores does your processor have?
   1
   2
   4
   8

2.5. What brand processor do you use?
   AMD
   Intel
   Cyrix
   PowerPC
   Other

3.What timer interrupt frequency do you prefer?
   Dynamic (only on machines with good bios)
   1000hz
   864hz
   432hz (dual cores only)
   other (suggest)

4. What do you prefer out of the following?
   Normal desktop/laptop settings
   Low-Latency settings (CFQ, and others)
   other (suggest)

5. If I were to write shellscripts that would allow you to download the    source, copy a config file, allow you to play with the settings, and build the kernel, would you use it?
  Yes
  No
  I will write the scripts for you

6.Do you have any suggestions? If so, please send them along. I want patch suggestions, code contributions, anything you can throw at me. If it's really a good submission, I'm sure Waninkoko would consider adding it to the patchset. If you know how to make the kernel any smaller without impacting stability, functionality, hardware support, or speed, please let me know. I currently remove all debugging symbols, nonessential debugging system, and other junk...I need to know what other junk can be safely removed.

---

### Post by ilikenwf on 2007-12-10
D'oh! I misnamed the x86_64 kernel again...for some reason, amd64 is appened to the end of it...don't worry...it doesn't mean anything. I removed that from the deb file names to prevent worry.

-------------------------------------------------------
**Changes - 2.6.24-rc4-zen1 - Released 12/10/07**
-------------------------------------------------------
Applied fix for the nVidia/ATI driver kernel issue that is allowing us to keep preemptible RCU
Fixed ATI/nVidia kernel module compilation problems
Set maximum number of processor cores to 8 so that multi-cores are all supported
Removed plenty of seemingly useless items, some may be needed, but those users can compile on their own or notify me and I can re-enable them
Trimmed Fat (see [changelog]("http://www.mattparnell.com/zen/changelog"))

Please answer the questions in my previous post. Anybody here good with shellscript?

Muty-bg will surely have the x86 version up at some soon point. (Btw Muty...I already did that little hack you found to this code, so preemptible RCU will work with nVidia and ATI)

### Post by Lord Illidan on 2007-12-10
Since the ipw3945 microcode is already installed under Ubuntu (Restricted Drivers), does one have to reinstall them for them to work with the new kernel?

---

### Post by ilikenwf on 2007-12-10
> **Lord Illidan said:**
> Since the ipw3945 microcode is already installed under Ubuntu (Restricted Drivers), does one have to reinstall them for them to work with the new kernel?

You can use those with a tiny hack...just make a symlink in /lib/firmware between the ubuntu kernel's folder...make sure that you name the link 2.6.24-rc4-zen1-whatever...

```
ln -s /lib/firmware/2.6.22-14-generic /lib/firmware/2.6.24-rc4-zen1-whatever

```
then, you should have these in /lib/firmware:
2.6.22-14-generic (whatever it's named...)
2.6.24-rc4-zen1-whatever

Then, just update your initramfs, or just do a 
```
dpkg-reconfigure linux-image-2.6.24-rc4-zen1-whateveryouusehere
```

Then, reboot. It should work, provided you get the names correct.

---

### Post by ilikenwf on 2007-12-10
I will add it to the top post too, but I have squashed the nVidia side of the bug! I forgot about this, but nVidia's current driver release doesn't work with 2.6.24...so...you need to install the beta version, which is stable.

[http://www.nvidia.com/Download/betadrivers.aspx?lang=en-us](http://www.nvidia.com/Download/betadrivers.aspx?lang=en-us)

### Post by Muty-bg on 2007-12-11
OK I'll write a quick and dirty guide how to compile the sources. Btw we were discussing with ilikenwf the possibility of making a bash script for compiling the sources. Maybe it's really a good idea. 

ok so here it goes:

```
sudo -i
cd /usr/src/
wget http://www.mattparnell.com/zen/2.6.24-rc4-zen1/linux-2.6.24-rc4-zen1.tar.bz2
tar xvjf linux-2.6.24-rc4-zen1.tar.bz2
ln -s zen-sources linux
cd linux
wget http://www.mattparnell.com/zen/2.6.24-rc4-zen1/config/x8664generic
mv x8664generic .config 
INSTALL_MOD_STRIP=1 CONCURRENCY_LEVEL=4 CC="gcc-4.1 -Os -funit-at-a-time -mregparm=3" make-kpkg --initrd kernel_image kernel_headers --append-to-version=-yourversionhere
```

---

### Post by Megaton on 2007-12-13
Posted here for anyone else to use and/or suggestions.

Fire up the all-powerful terminal
cd /usr/src
sudo -i
wget [http://www.mattparnell.com/zen/2.6.24-rc5-zen0/linux-2.6.24-rc5-zen0.tar.bz2](http://www.mattparnell.com/zen/2.6.24-rc5-zen0/linux-2.6.24-rc5-zen0.tar.bz2)
tar xvjf linux-2.6.24-rc5-zen0.tar.bz2
rm -rf linux && ln -s zen-sources linux
cd linux
cp /boot/config-`uname -r` .config && make oldconfig
make xconfig

Save your config and stop for a second.
If you have Zen deb's installed, use synaptic to do a complete removal
If you have any Zen .deb's in /usr/src, delete them.  (rm -rf *.deb)
if you have a Zen folder in /lib/modules, remove it

make sure you are back in /usr/src/linux
INSTALL_MOD_STRIP=1 CONCURRENCY_LEVEL=4 CC="gcc-4.1 -Os -funit-at-a-time -mregparm=3" make-kpkg --initrd kernel_image kernel_headers
cd /lib/firmware
ln -s /lib/firmware/2.6.22-14-generic 2.6.24-rc5-zen0
ls (make sure the softlink is there)
cd /usr/src
dpkg -i *.deb

once they are installed:
gedit /boot/grub/menu.lst
If it is good to go then exit, exit root, exit terminal, reboot (i take out quiet and splash on the kernel line)

choose the new zen kernel
at the login screen, hit ctrl+alt+f1
at this terminal, login
sudo /etc/init.d/gdm stop
cd (to the directory where you put NVIDIA-Linux****.run
sudo sh NVIDIA-Linux*****.run
after exit: sudo /etc/X11/xorg.conf to make sure all is well
sudo /etc/init.d/gdm start
you should see an nVidia beta logo and the login screen

Remeber when starting and stopping the display manager, use yours:
gdm - gnome
kdm - kde
xdm - xfce

---

### Post by ilikenwf on 2007-12-14
I just built a new version, and all ACPI is working, including reboot...may have finally found another golden snapshot build...

I also wrote and submitted a couple of patches to Waninkoko to see if he will add them to the Zen set...one of them is an option to strip debugging symbols for everyone (for people who don't have automagic compile scripts like make-kpkg), and the other adds a 216hz clock interrupt option for quad-core users who want the supposedly optimal rate of 864hz total.

I can do patches...sometimes...but I am not the best at complicated shellscripts...so, here's what I can think of that a script would need in order for regular users to compile from source...
```
[LIST=1]
[*]wget source and a generic config file from mattparnell.com/zen/

[*]make sure current version of gcc, as well as other dependencies installed

[*] Ask user who cpu manufacturer is. Make appropriate change to .config

[*]Ask user how many cores they have. Select appropriate hz option, and turn on/off SMP, hyperthreading, etc..

[*]Ask user if they would like to make additional configuration changes, if so, run xconfig (so they can add/remove modules and such to reduce compile time)

[*]Ask user if they want kernel headers, modules built...

[*]Ask users if they are ready to build

[*]Build the kernel using the concurrency option (and possibly mod strip if my current patch isn't accepted)

[*]Ask if user wants debs installed

[*]Install debs

[*]Modify /boot/grub/menu.lst for tuxonice (ask user where swap location is)

[*]Possbly ask user if they want to install nvidia or ati drivers...also, remind user to reboot into new kernel and make install ndiswrapper if need be...
[/LIST]
```

---

### Post by garoth2 on 2007-12-14
Compiling the rc5-zen0 kernel from source and applying the fix ( [http://gentoo-wiki.com/HOWTO_ATI_Drivers#Build_ati-drivers_on_rt-kernels_failed](http://gentoo-wiki.com/HOWTO_ATI_Drivers#Build_ati-drivers_on_rt-kernels_failed) ), I am able to compile the fglrx 7.11 drivers (using envy).

I've attached my config file. Note:

-Uses SLAB allocator. With this I am able to suspend to RAM, but I can't successfully wakeup from RAM - I haven't tried to fix this yet, though, and I know it's a whole other issue
-Setup for single-core AMD64 processor (no SMP support)

If you want the debs then let me know...!

Aside: One issue I've been having since trying 2.6.24 are occasional system stalls... they occur I'd say every 5-10 minutes and last 1-2 seconds. It's not such a major deal when doing most tasks, but it's annoying when watching video. Anyone else experiencing this? I really don't know where to start debugging this - my system logs don't seem to update with any new information after the stalls.

-Uses SLAB allocator. With this I am able to suspend to RAM, but I can't successfully wakeup from RAM - I haven't tried to fix this yet, though, and I know it's a whole other issue
-Setup for single-core AMD64 processor (no SMP support)

If you want the debs then let me know...!

Aside: One issue I've been having since trying 2.6.24 are occasional system stalls... they occur I'd say every 5-10 minutes and last 1-2 seconds. It's not such a major deal when doing most tasks, but it's annoying when watching video. Anyone else experiencing this? I really don't know where to start debugging this - my system logs don't seem to update with any new information after the stalls.

Hmmmm. OK I'll try this again. Maybe I messed up something. Sorry but I had birthday this week and things are abit messy around me lately.

### Post by ilikenwf on 2007-12-15
> **Muty-bg said:**
> Hmmmm. OK I'll try this again. Maybe I messed up something. Sorry but I had birthday this week and things are abit messy around me lately.

Don't worry...your birthday is more important than kernel development!

Oh...and...enable soft and hard irqs in the processor options, as well as preemptible rcu. Also, in the cfs config set it to highly interactive desktop, and turn on low latency settings for everything...


Also, my patches were added...there is one that appends the -s KBUILD flag to strip debugging symbols, which allows everyone to do that to reduce kernel size (enable that one too...)

Oh...and our current compile command has been redundant...you should type only this:
```
INSTALL_MOD_STRIP=1 CONCURRENCY_LEVEL=2 sudo make-kpkg --initrd kernel_image kernel_headers --append-to-version=-x86-64
```

And, with my new strip debugging symbols patch, I'm not sure if INSTALL_MOD_STRIP=1 is needed or not...I haven't tested it yet.

The other of my patches adds a 216hz frequency so that quad-core users can have the total of the optimal 864hz...

---

compiled the sources for my laptop (my main reason for trying to get the .24 kernel was for tickless support) and notice that power consumption is higher than on the stock gutsy kernel. powertop shows 8.2% C0 state surfing the web, with about 300-500 wakeups--2 of the top causes of wakeups are "kernel-core", which isn't the case with the vanilla kernel.  using a hacked fedora 2.6.23 kernel, wps was ~120. i have timer freq set to 300ms.

i'm also unable to set iwpriv controls using an iwl3945 NIC.  it shows up as "wlan0_rename", 
```
iwpriv wlan0_rename get_power
wlan0_rename  no private ioctls.

```

on the bright side...
the new nvidia beta driver compiled without a hitch against the sources, and the brightness now works great (thinkpad r61).
using slub, suspend to ram works like a champ (haven't tried hibernate yet).

i might try a make oldconfig with the vanilla kernel and see whether it's a settings or kernel issue with power consumption.

### Post by ilikenwf on 2007-12-16
Hey Muty-bg...you rock..hope this doesn't take too much of your time. Next time you compile (this isn't critical, so don't worry about it right now) disable the option "Optimize for Size." I read that it only enables the gcc flag -Os, and without it -O2 is the default, and O2 is supposedly faster....

Also, because my patch adds the -s option in config under Strip Debugging Symbols, we don't actually need to type in the INSTALL_MOD_STRIP=1 anymore...I tried it both ways and no size difference...so that's all MOD_STRIP is.

---

---

### Post by Heazky on 2007-12-17
> **Lord Illidan said:**
> So how do I get it working then? Just put the firmware somewhere and hope for the best? Will network manager work with it?

ilikenwf's config has the iwlwifi enabled, so you just need to put the firmware into /lib/firmware/`uname -r`. If it isn't enabled in your kernel: you can enable the driver in 'Device Drivers -> Wireless', then recompile your kernel
The answer to your second question is also 'yes': it does work with network manager.

---

oh yea ndiswrapper doesn't work either.. but one thing at a time

BTW, i have a wifi adapter with the same chipset and I am able to simply use the module provided in the kernel.  I am running rc4-zen0.  I don't need to use ndiswrapper either and I seem to get full bandwidth.  I simply set up the login information (I am using WPA2) in the /etc/network/interfaces file as such:

```
auto wlan0
iface wlan0 inet dhcp
wpa-driver wext
wpa-ssid YOUR SSID
wpa-ap-scan 1
wpa-proto WPA RSN
wpa-pairwise TKIP CCMP
wpa-group TKIP CCMP
wpa-key-mgmt WPA-PSK
wpa-psk YOUR HEX KEY FOR THE WIRELESS NETWORK
```

I used the following thread to help set up interfaces file: [http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=318539](http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=318539)

HTH.

---

### Post by ilikenwf on 2007-12-18
NEW VERSiON!

I am building...and I have done some more config tweaking +trying some different things...the image may be bigger this time, and I am testing it this way with some new KBUILD_CFLAGS. I will release an AMD64 version at some point, too...
And if you want it to be even faster, build it yourself for just your system, and the drivers for your devices (except for sound and the other huge ones) build as part of the kernel, and not as modules.
Hey Muty-bg...try my config the next time you compile, just enable the 32 bit specific stuff...

64 Bit Debs:
[http://www.mattparnell.com/zen/2.6.24-rc5-zen1/64%20bit/linux-headers-2.6.24-rc5-zen1-x86-64-o2_2.6.24-rc5-zen1-x86-64-o2-10.00.Custom_amd64.deb](http://www.mattparnell.com/zen/2.6.24-rc5-zen1/64%20bit/linux-headers-2.6.24-rc5-zen1-x86-64-o2_2.6.24-rc5-zen1-x86-64-o2-10.00.Custom_amd64.deb)
[http://www.mattparnell.com/zen/2.6.24-rc5-zen1/64%20bit/linux-image-2.6.24-rc5-zen1-x86-64-o2_2.6.24-rc5-zen1-x86-64-o2-10.00.Custom_amd64.deb](http://www.mattparnell.com/zen/2.6.24-rc5-zen1/64%20bit/linux-image-2.6.24-rc5-zen1-x86-64-o2_2.6.24-rc5-zen1-x86-64-o2-10.00.Custom_amd64.deb)
64 Bit Ndiswrapper kernel module (put it in /lib/modules/linux/2.6.24-rc5-zen1-x86-64-o2/misc and make sure to run the ndiswrapper commands to install it to be probed at boot time...): [http://www.mattparnell.com/zen/2.6.24-rc5-zen1/64%20bit/ndiswrapper.ko](http://www.mattparnell.com/zen/2.6.24-rc5-zen1/64%20bit/ndiswrapper.ko)

Source:
rc5-zen1 source is up: [http://www.mattparnell.com/zen/2.6.24-rc5-zen1/linux-2.6.24-rc5-zen1.tar.bz2](http://www.mattparnell.com/zen/2.6.24-rc5-zen1/linux-2.6.24-rc5-zen1.tar.bz2)
config: [http://www.mattparnell.com/zen/2.6.24-rc5-zen1/config](http://www.mattparnell.com/zen/2.6.24-rc5-zen1/config)

### Post by mma8x on 2007-12-20
first time since i've had (well, almost) everything working. thinkpad r61 using gutsy.  i haven't been able to boot the zen deb for quite a while--i get a strange memory error right on boot.  machine then hangs; it doesn't even get to boot into the ramdisk image or anything.  soooo, i recompiled, and now:
iwl3945 driver is working--i'm not able to set/list iwpriv (see earlier post), but i'm able to set power conservation with 
```
echo 7 > /sys/bus/pci/drivers/iwl3945/0000\:03\:00.0/power_level

```, which only draws .1W at idle.  firmware installed to /lib/firmware.
nvidia drivers: using beta driver, works great.  brightness controls via hardware work no problem.  i was also unable to compile this module against the zen headers; no problem using source files.
suspend/hibernate! yup, both working.  in /etc/default/acpi-support, i have POST_VIDEO and SET_VBE_STATE set to false.  note that this took an as-yet-undefined kernel config tweak to get it going--i couldn't get it to work with the last set of sources; this one i don't know what i did different, esp since i started with the same config file.

now, at idle with screen at max dim, i'm using 13.0W.  more user-friendly screen brightness and moderate web-surfing gives me 16W.  i've attached my config file; sorry zen guys if i've changed your settings beyond recognition.  also, note that this will probably only work on a thinkpad; i stripped it down pretty good.  maybe people can figure out why mine's working.  

WHOOPS! i take it back--my config file is 75k, which is too big to upload.  if anyone knows where else i can post it, lmk.

### Post by Muty-bg on 2007-12-20
> **XVampireX said:**
> Hi, I just wanted to let everyone here know that I successfully installed the nvidia beta driver this time around, but with the ubuntu stock kernel. However, I still can't do so with the Zen Kernel, I've posted to this thread on nvnews:
[http://www.nvnews.net/vbulletin/showthread.php?p=1487093](http://www.nvnews.net/vbulletin/showthread.php?p=1487093)

If this problem could be fixed, it would be really great!

HI this a known problem. There are some file files missing in the linux-headers, that are needed in order to compile the driver. We'll fix that. 

For now the quickest way for you will be to compile the module against the kernel sources. Here is how you can do it:

sudo -i
cd /usr/src/
wget [http://www.mattparnell.com/zen/2.6.24-rc5-zen1/linux-2.6.24-rc5-zen1.tar.bz2](http://www.mattparnell.com/zen/2.6.24-rc5-zen1/linux-2.6.24-rc5-zen1.tar.bz2)
tar xvjf linux-2.6.24-rc5-zen1.tar.bz2
cd zen-sources
wget [http://www.mattparnell.com/zen/2.6.24-rc5-zen1/config](http://www.mattparnell.com/zen/2.6.24-rc5-zen1/config)
mv config .config
sh NVIDIA-*.run --kernel-name=zen-sources

This should do the trick. Let me know if you have troubles

EDIT: aaaahh oops. You are using nvidia, I wrote it for ati. Anyway I'm not shure for the last command since I don't have an nvidia card around me to test it. Let me know if it doesn't work.

### Post by ilikenwf on 2007-12-20
AMD64 Version is now up!

[http://www.mattparnell.com/zen/2.6.24-rc5-zen1/AMD64/](http://www.mattparnell.com/zen/2.6.24-rc5-zen1/AMD64/)

Note that this one disables C1E to allow use of Dynticks and High Resolution timers. I have compiled it with special buildflags, and removed Early Printk.

To re-enable C1E and lose Dynticks and HR Timers, add this boot parameter:
force_amd_c1e

Try it!

       does not exist.  The most likely reason for this is that the kernel
       source files in '/usr/src/zen-sources' have not been configured.

       '/var/log/nvidia-installer.log' for details.  You may find suggestions
       on fixing installation problems in the README available on the Linux
       driver download page at www.nvidia.com.
```

OK sorry. It won't work if you don't have the kernel compiled.
So what will do the trick is to actually have the kernel compiled. It will take some time but it will defenetly work

anwyay here's what you should do

```
cd /usr/src/zen-sources
CONCURRENCY_LEVEL=4 CC="gcc-4.1 -funit-at-a-time -mregparm=3" sudo make-kpkg --initrd kernel_image kernel_headers --append-to-version=-x86
```

OK this will take you about an hour or something. You don't need to install the resulting debs, You already have them installed so now run again:

```
sh NVIDIA-*.run --kernel-name=zen-sources
```

This should do the trick
Let me know if you still have problems.

### Post by mikeyakame on 2007-12-25
just wanted to say what a nice piece of work this custom kernel is. I have it running stripped down as minimally as possible, compiled from source code on debian. it runs really well, to be honest it's much more stable than the .23 stable branch of the kernel! I have it running in a server environment with high data throughput, and after tweaking tcp, vm and all that fun stuff for its specific use. It multi threads great with SMP, and the CFS seems to work extraordinarily well. Especially when you set NIC irq affinity per core/cpu for multiple NIC's. Also boot time is amazingly quick, and works great with cryptsetup. 

Very nice piece of work, just though i'd say thanks and add my experience ;)

---

### Post by ilikenwf on 2007-12-26
Okay... rc6-zen0 source is up, and so are the updated config files...the 64 bit config files will work for 32 bit, just make sure to choose the correct cpu settings...if you use an amd chip, choose amd64, if you use intel or other, choose x86_64. I'm building the AMD64 Version now, and will build x86_64 after that. Muty-bg can build on his own time, or you can compile...make sure to see the **[changelog]("http://www.mattparnell.com/zen/changelog")** for the updates.

Source: 
[http://www.mattparnell.com/zen/2.6.24-rc6-zen0/linux-2.6.24-rc6-zen0.tar.bz2](http://www.mattparnell.com/zen/2.6.24-rc6-zen0/linux-2.6.24-rc6-zen0.tar.bz2)

Config:
[http://www.mattparnell.com/zen/2.6.24-rc6-zen0/config/](http://www.mattparnell.com/zen/2.6.24-rc6-zen0/config/)\


Until I can get the madwifi to compile, I won't upload any releases...it should be between today and tomorrow...madwifi is having a fit...

### Post by hacker1 on 2007-12-28
After installing the kernel on my AMD64 machine, I get the following error at boot:

```
Setting up cryptographic volume root (based on /dev/hdc2)
cryptsetup: Source device /dev/hdc2 not found
```

Cryptsetup is working nicely with the Ubuntu 2.6.22 and hardy 2.6.24 kernel.

---

### Post by ilikenwf on 2007-12-28
> **hacker1 said:**
> After installing the kernel on my AMD64 machine, I get the following error at boot:

```
Setting up cryptographic volume root (based on /dev/hdc2)
cryptsetup: Source device /dev/hdc2 not found
```

Cryptsetup is working nicely with the Ubuntu 2.6.22 and hardy 2.6.24 kernel.

I just can't figure out, why cryptsetup seems to be unable to find /dev/hdc2 using the zen kernel.

The kernel module may not be compatible...

As for the dpkg problem...just make an empty directory in /lib/modules for that kernel...

```
sudo mkdir /lib/modules/2.6.24-rc5-zen1-x86
```

Then things should work again.

### Post by Gigamo on 2008-01-12
Is there any way to install/try this kernel without a swap partition? :) I installed ubuntu without swap, and in the install guide it says that "You must specifiy your swap partition" :D

---

### Post by binary.koala on 2008-01-12
> **Gigamo said:**
> Is there any way to install/try this kernel without a swap partition? :) I installed ubuntu without swap, and in the install guide it says that "You must specifiy your swap partition" :D

hi, instead of using swap partition you can use swap-file (windows like!)
for that:

1. create a swap file (here aprox 1gb, takes a minute to create):
```
sudo dd if=/dev/zero of=/swapfile bs=1024 count=1024000
```
2. initialize it as swap:
```
sudo mkswap /swapfile
```
3. add as swap:
```
sudo swapon /swapfile
```
4. add swap to fstab:
```
sudo sh -c 'echo "/swapfile none swap sw 0 0" >> /etc/fstab'
```

i hope it helps.

---

### Post by Gigamo on 2008-01-12
> **binary.koala said:**
> hi, instead of using swap partition you can use swap-file (windows like!)
for that:

1. create a swap file (here aprox 1gb, takes a minute to create):
```
sudo dd if=/dev/zero of=/swapfile bs=1024 count=1024000
```2. initialize it as swap:
```
sudo mkswap /swapfile
```3. add as swap:
```
sudo swapon /swapfile
```4. add swap to fstab:
```
sudo sh -c 'echo "/swapfile none swap sw 0 0" >> /etc/fstab'
```i hope it helps.

---

### Post by binary.koala on 2008-01-12
> **binary.koala said:**
> ok, here is something worth trying, sounds reasonable at least:
[http://www.freesoftwaremagazine.com/articles/hibernate_linux?page=0%2C3](http://www.freesoftwaremagazine.com/articles/hibernate_linux?page=0%2C3)

however here is some bad news:

> * Hibernation needs swap
The hibernation feature (suspend-to-disk) writes out the contents of the memory to the swap partition before turning off the machine. Therefore, your swap partition should be at least as big as your RAM size. The hibernation implementation currently used in Ubuntu, swsusp, needs a swap or suspend partition, and can not use a swap file on an active file system.



[https://help.ubuntu.com/community/SwapFaq](https://help.ubuntu.com/community/SwapFaq)

i would assume Xen kernel is using swsusp as i was not able to ```
 cat /proc/suspend2/headerlocations
```

### Post by sjust on 2008-01-22
I followed the guide I posted awhile back and built my own deb package.
sam@samstoy:~$uname -a
Linux samstoy 2.6.24-rc5-zen1.1216 #1 SMP PREEMPT Wed Jan 16 17:01:32 EST 2008 i686 GNU/Linux
I did not use fakeroot or was adding myself to the src group any help as there wasn't one. I just used sudo and the nautilus scripts  that I have installed to open files as root. 
I downloaded the source from the first post and built the package. I used envy to install the graphics driver "nvida". When I did make menuconfig I compared it to the one on the first post and made sure it was set up for 32 bit. There are a few things that do not work right like system sounds but most are trivial for me. I think there is a newer source might try it and see if it works.

### Post by Muty-bg on 2008-02-01
OK I've uploaded them again. With these headers the at and nvidia drivers should install just fine :)

[linux-headers]("http://www.mattparnell.com/zen/2.6.24-zen1/x86/linux-headers-2.6.24-zen1-x86_0.1-1_i386.deb")

NOTE: I'm not shure if I added a script to change the softlink location. 
so check /usr/src/ and if the linux link doesn't point to linux-headers-2.6.24-zen1-x86 then type these:

```
rm /usr/src/linux
ln -s /usr/src/linux-headers-2.6.24-zen1-x86 /usr/src/linux
```

That should do it. Let me know if it works now pls :)

---

### Post by Ctrl+Alt+Del on 2008-02-05
in short:
fire up your favorite editor and edit the required lines in /boot/grub/menu.lst.
The exact filenames you have to enter can seen via ls /boot
you should end up with a few lines looking like this:

title           Ubuntu 7.10, kernel 2.6.24-zen1-x86
root            (hd0,1)
kernel          /boot/vmlinuz-2.6.24-zen1-x86 root=UUID=58e20ffd-7ba2-4022-b684-7366bc77370b ro resume=/dev/sda5
initrd          /boot/initrd.img-2.6.24-zen1-x86
quiet

I am not going to get into more detail here, i think anyone installing a custom kernel should have a basic idea how his grub config looks ;)

Note: this will enable you to boot that kernel, but it is by no means a "real fix" as apt still has the non-finished configuration in it's database and will therefore rerun it every time you want to install a package. a fixed package is still required. I had a quick look at the postinstall script only to find out that it is a lot more complicated than i anticipated it to be. I may have a look at it later and try to fix it, but my scripting skills are VERY limited. I'd prefer having t fixed by someone who actually knows what he's doing

---

       kernel headers) were installed, you may need to specify
       their location with the SYSSRC environment variable or
       the equivalent nvidia-installer command line option.
ERROR: Installation has failed.  Please see the file
       '/var/log/nvidia-installer.log' for details.  You may find suggestions
       on fixing installation problems in the README available on the Linux
       driver download page at [www.nvidia.com](www.nvidia.com).

### Post by bornagainpenguin on 2008-02-13
> **Ctrl+Alt+Del said:**
> in short:
fire up your favorite editor and edit the required lines in /boot/grub/menu.lst.
The exact filenames you have to enter can seen via ls /boot
you should end up with a few lines looking like this:

title           Ubuntu 7.10, kernel 2.6.24-zen1-x86
root            (hd0,1)
kernel          /boot/vmlinuz-2.6.24-zen1-x86 root=UUID=58e20ffd-7ba2-4022-b684-7366bc77370b ro resume=/dev/sda5
initrd          /boot/initrd.img-2.6.24-zen1-x86
quiet

I am not going to get into more detail here, i think anyone installing a custom kernel should have a basic idea how his grub config looks ;)

Note: this will enable you to boot that kernel, but it is by no means a "real fix" as apt still has the non-finished configuration in it's database and will therefore rerun it every time you want to install a package. a fixed package is still required. I had a quick look at the postinstall script only to find out that it is a lot more complicated than i anticipated it to be. I may have a look at it later and try to fix it, but my scripting skills are VERY limited. I'd prefer having t fixed by someone who actually knows what he's doing

THANK YOU!

This and fixing some issues I was having with my swap fixed my hibernation!

--bornagainpenguin

### Post by ilikenwf on 2008-02-23
> **addisor said:**
> I installed "Envy" through my existing ubuntu kernel and gui, then booted in zen safe mode, ran envy -t, loaded nvidia driver. then ran ubuntu kernel and loaded latest nvidia driver manually through envy. Then went for a normal boot on zen, hangs as stated. never really touched X11/xorg.conf. is it worth showing you x11/xorg.conf as seen from zen recovery mode?
my original ubuntu set up got a bit messed up due zen install and i have had to fiddle with the X11 there.

Reboot into safe mode, and

sudo vim /etc/X11/xorg.conf

What I meant to do after Envy was to get the 169.07 driver package, and manually install it. But I see a totally new build has leaked, 171.05 . Try that first, if it doesn't work, use 169.07. Reboot into safe mode and do this:

```
sudo wget http://ftp.icm.edu.pl/packages/linux-nvidia/Linux-x86_64/171.05/NVIDIA-Linux-x86_64-171.05-pkg2.run
sudo sh NVIDIA-Linux-x86_64-171.05-pkg2.run
install and say yes to everything
Reboot
```

If that doesn't work, try [169.07]("http://ftp.icm.edu.pl/packages/linux-nvidia/Linux-x86_64/169.07/NVIDIA-Linux-x86_64-169.07-pkg2.run")

x86 Drivers are available, but zen3 isn't built for that yet anyway.

### Post by xanikseo on 2008-02-23
Should work with " apt-get install build-essential linux-headers-`uname -r` " as far as I know... I think I have GCC 4.1 though

To get the git sources:
cd /usr/src 
sudo -s
git clone git://repo.or.cz/linux-2.6/zen-sources.git

And compile (just in case you don't know):
cd zen-sources
make oldconfig #(hit enter at all options for default)
make xconfig #configure kernel all you wish (shouldn't need to do so)
make-kpkg clean
make-kpkg --initrd --revision=386 kernel_image kernel_headers modules_image

---

### Post by ilikenwf on 2008-02-23
> **xanikseo said:**
> Should work with " apt-get install build-essential linux-headers-`uname -r` " as far as I know... I think I have GCC 4.1 though

To get the git sources:
cd /usr/src 
sudo -s
git clone git://repo.or.cz/linux-2.6/zen-sources.git

And compile (just in case you don't know):
cd zen-sources
make oldconfig #(hit enter at all options for default)
make xconfig #configure kernel all you wish (shouldn't need to do so)
make-kpkg clean
make-kpkg --initrd --revision=386 kernel_image kernel_headers modules_image

Not quite...

```
sudo apt-get install build-essential kernel-package
```

No need for ubuntu headers. 

For the source, you can just download my tarball...it's faster. If you do use git, you can always be up to date by using git pull and recompiling. For compiling, if you just copy my config from here, and then build, it will save you lots of time. You may want to "make menuconfig" if you need to change the architecture from AMD64 to x86, x86_64, or any other, after copying and renaming AMD64.config to .config. My config is by far the fastest configuration of this kernel possible. I will have to revamp the CFLAGS, though, soon.

```

cd /usr/src
sudo wget http://www.mattparnell.com/zen/2.6.24-zen3/linux-2.6.24-zen3.tar.bz2
sudo tar xjvf linux-2.6.24-zen3.tar.bz2
cd zen-sources
wget http://www.mattparnell.com/zen/2.6.24-zen3/config/AMD64.config
sudo mv AMD64.config .config
sudo make-kpkg clean
INSTALL_MOD_STRIP=1 CONCURRENCY=2 sudo make-kpkg --initrd --append-to-version=-whateveryouwant kernel_image kernel_headers modules_image
```

When done, go back to /usr/src, and install the debs. Then run the nVidia or ATI installer. I'll write an easy shellscript sometime to help everyone do this.

---

### Post by ilikenwf on 2008-02-29
Try using Envy. If that doesn't work, it's the classic bug that we've been fighting for the longest time.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

That said, I'm happy to release what I would call a test build of** _2.6.25_-rc3-zen0** . It fixes many bugs for me, as I am now able to boot with no special grub parameters (no disabling anything! yay!)...

The only caveats/problems are that the following kernel modules don't compile:
madwifi/atheros devices
the Ralink rt2x00
aufs
unionfs
chunkfs

If you try this kernel, you'll end up having to use ndiswrapper unless you can get the svn drivers to compile on your own for those wireless devices. Filesystem support is likely to be fixed very soon, as are the wifi drivers.

Download it here: [http://www.mattparnell.com/zen/2.6.25-rc3-zen0/AMD64/](http://www.mattparnell.com/zen/2.6.25-rc3-zen0/AMD64/)

On a side note, I'll try to speed the x86_64 and i386 builds out asap.

I have created a Wiki page, although I haven't filled everything in yet. If any of you would like to help me move the info from the first post over to the Wiki with nice formatting, it would be greatly appreciated. [https://wiki.ubuntu.com/ZenKernel](https://wiki.ubuntu.com/ZenKernel)

---

### Post by andreya on 2008-03-03
Hi!

Here is my experience of testing zen kernel.

I have Compaq laptop with ATI Radeon 9200 on board.
My ordinary system is Gutsy with generic kernel.

At first I tried 2.6.24-zen1 kernel since it has prebuilt deb packages.
But after installing I've got compiz and all DRI stuff not working.
Envy did not helped me since my videocard is too legacy:) - it reported that has no suitable drivers. Although default opensource ATI drivers works fine in Gutsy.
The reason default driver was failed with zen1 was the kernel has no AGPGART module in hand.

So I was forced to download kernel sources (at this time zen3) and heve built kernel with some minor tuning (cpu type, enabling agpgart and disabling some wireless drivers which caused compilation to fail - 2 or 3 items).

After all I've got everything working, at least X with compiz, sound, sata drives and wireless nework. 
My early experience is that zen3 boots slightly slower (but it has all drivers) and works slightly faster than generic 2.6.22 kernel.

wbr,
Andrey

---

### Post by rockin_goliath on 2008-03-03
I don't mean to sound impolite, I just want to learn more about what the Zen Ubuntu kernel is. If it is faster, more stable, and has more hardware support, why isn't it being used as the main kernel for Ubuntu? What are the advantages/trade offs of using this kernel instead of the main one? Are there plans to merge the good changes in the Zen kernel with the main one? Thanks!

---

### Post by ilikenwf on 2008-03-03
Thanks for letting me know! I'll enable the ATI modules for you, next time!

> **rockin_goliath said:**
> I don't mean to sound impolite, I just want to learn more about what the Zen Ubuntu kernel is. If it is faster, more stable, and has more hardware support, why isn't it being used as the main kernel for Ubuntu? What are the advantages/trade offs of using this kernel instead of the main one? Are there plans to merge the good changes in the Zen kernel with the main one? Thanks!

It isn't being used in the default Ubuntu distributions because of bureaucracy, mostly. They have a "kernel freeze" for each release of Ubuntu, and Gutsy is frozen at 2.6.22. The Ubuntu devs do their best to make a stable kernel with all the hardware it can possibly support. The thing is they don't use bleeding edge kernel versions, due to the freeze. This can reduce speed, and hardware support, as well as leave old bugs in the kernel. The Zen kernel fixes this by adding all sorts of bug fixes, drivers, and other miscellanea that enhance the kernel to be faster, stable, and all around better. The advantages are speed, stablity, security, better hardware support, and other such things. The additions in the Zen kernel are somewhat merged into later Ubuntu kernels, with a few glaring omissions. It just takes time. You won't see any similar features in default kernels until you either switch to Hardy, or it goes gold. Coincidentally, this kernel is still probably better than the default Hardy kernel.

----------------

That all said, I am happy to release the newest non-testing/stable version of the Zen kernel, 2.6.24-zen4. I haven't built for x86_64 or AMD64 yet, but I have an i386 machine setup now on ssh via remote and built the packages for i386, as I feel I have neglegeted the x86 users recently. I have also included the nvidia kernel module deb package this time to see if that will fix the nVidia driver errors. ATI people, let me know if you want me to do the same for you.

**_TRY IT NOW!_**

2.6.24-zen4 i386 builds: [http://www.mattparnell.com/zen/2.6.24-zen4/i386/](http://www.mattparnell.com/zen/2.6.24-zen4/i386/)

---

### Post by RavanH on 2008-03-05
TIP for the Wiki:

Include instructions for those using Grub2 (instead of default Grub).

Suggested text:

Edit (as root) your /etc/default/grub file BEFORE installing the kernel, and find the line starting with GRUB_CMDLINE_LINUX= (probably the last line). Ad just before the closing quote resume=/dev/[Insert Swap Location here] so it will automatically be added each time you install a kernel. If you do this after the kernel is installed, be sure to run the command update-grub in terminal (as root) to make the change propagate to the kernel boot list.

---

### Post by ilikenwf on 2008-03-11
> **gplaxico said:**
> thanks for the reply.  :)

it is the intel ipw3945 wireless driver.  i am new to kernel compiling, and have scoured the internet to see how to do it with the zen sources with no luck...anyone with hints.

The driver is included in the Zen kernel. You need the device firmware, and need the option enabled in the wireless config. If in doubt, enable all wifi adapters. The precompiled packages all have it enabled. Once done and installed, just setup the firmware.

Howto from [http://ipw3945.sourceforge.net/](http://ipw3945.sourceforge.net/). You only need to check the option in the wireless config when you make xconfig, and then take care of the microcode, and daemon. Besides that, yo'll need the  WPA supplicant if you don't already have one...there are tutorials around for that. Everything else should be good. Once the firmware is in it's place (I don't know exactly where, but somewhere in /lib/firmware).
>  
n order to use the Intel PRO/Wireless 3945ABG Network Connection driver for Linux you will need the following:

   1. The binary microcode image,[ available here.]("http://bughost.org/ipw3945/")
   2. The binary user space regulatory daemon, [available here]("http://bughost.org/ipw3945/").
   3. The ieee80211 subsystem version 1.1.11 or newer.
   4. Linux kernel 2.6.13 or newer. See README.ipw3945 for information on specific options required to be enabled in the kernel.
   5. Wireless Extensions (v17) and Tools (v28)
   6. For WPA you need a WPA supplicant compatible with the latest versions of the wireless extensions (v18 and newer). 

---

### Post by zenrox on 2008-03-11
my procudure i used to compile the zen kernel
 first i 
```

mkdir testing
git clone git://repo.or.cz/linux-2.6/zen-sources.git

```
this took entirly too long but any way
copyed and paste one of your config file in to ~/testing/zen-sources/.config
then
```

make xconfig 

```
proceded to configure for my cpu and arch
then
```

make kpkg clean
and
INSTALL_MOD_STRIP=1 CONCURRENCY_LEVEL=2 fakeroot make-kpkg --initrd kernel_image kernel_headers modules_image --revision=-whateveryouwant

```
note the fakeroot command 

i built it running its build as a user
and i built it on hardy using gcc4.2

The thing is that the nVidia sometimes decides not to work. Right now, the newest nVidia driver you can try is[ here]("http://www.nvidia.com/object/linux_display_ia32_171.06.html"). If it doesn't work, you'll want to edit /etc/X11/xorg.conf and replace (in the Driver section) the line that says Driver    "nvidia" to Driver "nv" That gives you the opensource version of the driver, vs the closed source version. Note that the opensource version does not do 3-d acceleration.

If you have a scan of that article, I'd love to see it!

### Post by taekr on 2008-03-14

---

### Post by ilikenwf on 2008-03-14
> **taekr said:**
> Sorry.. but..  what is nv??   I failed to install driver, latest driver from Nvidia. How can I use nv instead of Nvidia?

You understand you won't have 3-d acceleration support, right? If so, do the following:

CTRL + ALT + F3

login

```
sudo vim /etc/X11/xorg.conf
```

Use the page down button to scroll down to the following:
```

Section "Device"
	Identifier	"nVidia Corporation C51 [Geforce 6150 Go]"
**	Driver		"nvidia"**
	Busid		"PCI:0:5:0"
	Option		"sw_cursor"
```

Press the "I" key, and then scroll to the word "nvidia," and change it to "nv."

It should look like this (well...not exactly...but the driver line should look like the below emboldened line:)
```

Section "Device"
	Identifier	"nVidia Corporation C51 [Geforce 6150 Go]"
**	Driver		"nv"**
	Busid		"PCI:0:5:0"
	Option		"sw_cursor"
	
```

Then hit ": WQ" and hit enter (colon - W - Q - enter)

Then type startx and you should get a desktop.

---

Remove the deb package (nvidia). sudo dpkg -i nvidia-kernel-2.6.24-zen4_100.14.19.deb

Then, download this and put it somewhere (like your home folder):
[http://us.download.nvidia.com/XFree86/Linux-x86/169.12/NVIDIA-Linux-x86-169.12-pkg1.run](http://us.download.nvidia.com/XFree86/Linux-x86/169.12/NVIDIA-Linux-x86-169.12-pkg1.run)

Then go on to 

5.you need to run the installer. This needs to be done with GUI disabled, or they will refuse to install. Press Ctrl-Alt-F1 and bring up a full-screen terminal, then log in as you usually would. NOw run:

killall gdm && killall xinit
sudo ./<file name>.run

The installer should work.

### Post by ilikenwf on 2008-03-16

> **Achetar said:**
> That is correct. (and my WiFi is built in, not USB, sorry for not specifying).

Idea: You may have something wrong in /boot/grub/menu.lst. It is quite possible you are booting into recovery mode. Check that out. If it isn't the case, the other solution involves various symlinks. You could try this ([taken from here]("http://ubuntuforums.org/archive/index.php/t-89491.html")):

sudo apt-get update
sudo apt-get install sysv-rc-conf

After, run sudo sysv-rc-conf

For all of those that having HAL failure problem, try this:
1. change acpi-support from S to 2,3,4,5
2. change acpid from S to 2,3,4,5
3. change dbus from S to 2,3,4,5
4. Reboot. Go to the console and do ps -aef|grep hald. If hald service is up, then your dbus subsystem is running fine now. Try it.



> **Jasman said:**
> This should say "sudo dpkg -r...," no?

There are further instructions elsewhere (like the Nvidia site) for installing the nvidia-supplied drivers on Ubuntu.  I'd assume you should follow them to the letter.

Cloning the git tree allows you to type git pull when a new version of the kernel is out to download the newest sources, and it just updates the updated files, and keeps the unchanged ones. This is good if you plan on compiling as new releases come. Otherwise, choose the package download.

[The .config is here]("http://www.mattparnell.com/zen/2.6.24-zen4/x86_64/x86_64.config")... Just make sure to pick the correct processor type for your system. Outside of that, the optimal settings are already in place.

### Post by xanikseo on 2008-03-21
It's more likely that the VMWare module doesn't support the 2.6.24 linux kernel in general, rather than zen, unless zen has broken something (in most recent git).

### Post by ilikenwf on 2008-03-25
I would say it has something to do with the autoconf.h error that's messing with nVidia. 

Possible Fix: cd into your zen-sources directory, make a symbolic link between zen-sources (or the headers location)\include\linux\autoconf and include\linux\autoconf.h , that should silence this error.

Then, make a link between the zen-sources(or zen headers)\include\asm-x86 to zen-sources\include\asm

So, if you wanted to try this with your headers:

```

sudo ln -s \usr\src\linux-headers.2.6.24-zen4\include\linux\autoconf \usr\src\linux-headers.2.6.24-zen4\include\linux\autoconf.h
sudo ln -s \usr\src\linux-headers.2.6.24-zen4\include\asm-x86 \usr\src\linux-headers.2.6.24-zen4\include\asm

```

---

### Post by ilikenwf on 2008-03-25
For everyone just tuning in today, try this to get whatever modules you need compiled (nVidia, Virtualbox, etc...), and REPORT BACK!:
```

sudo ln -s \usr\src\linux-headers.2.6.24-zen4\include\linux\autoconf \usr\src\linux-headers.2.6.24-zen4\include\linux\autoconf.h
sudo ln -s \usr\src\linux-headers.2.6.24-zen4\include\asm-x86 \usr\src\linux-headers.2.6.24-zen4\include\asm

```

Deepclutch: You've already done the first one, try doing the second one now to fix the asm directory path. There may still be some paths messed up, but once we find them all this will be fixed for good!

---

### Post by tad1073 on 2008-03-27

### Post by ilikenwf on 2008-03-27
> **tad1073 said:**
> What is the equvilent to swappiness in 2.6.24-zen4

Take the value you used for swappiness and substract it from 100. 100 - swappiness value = mapped value

### Post by bornagainpenguin on 2008-04-03
Trying to update Ubuntu gets me this error message:

```
E: dpkg was interrupted, you must manually run 'dpkg --configure -a' to correct the problem. 
E: _cache->open() failed, please report.
```

Trying to run those commands in terminal gets me this response:

```
Setting up initramfs-tools (0.85eubuntu20) ...
update-initramfs: deferring update (trigger activated)

Processing triggers for initramfs-tools ...
update-initramfs: Generating /boot/initrd.img-2.6.24-zen1-x86
Cannot find /lib/modules/2.6.24-zen1-x86
update-initramfs: failed for /boot/initrd.img-2.6.24-zen1-x86
dpkg: subprocess post-installation script returned error exit status 1

```

And then dumps me back out to the command line.  Any ideas how I can fix this?

--bornagainpenguin

PS: NOTE: I am using an older build of zen.

---

### Post by ilikenwf on 2008-04-03
> **bornagainpenguin said:**
> Trying to update Ubuntu gets me this error message:

```
E: dpkg was interrupted, you must manually run 'dpkg --configure -a' to correct the problem. 
E: _cache->open() failed, please report.
```

Trying to run those commands in terminal gets me this response:

```
Setting up initramfs-tools (0.85eubuntu20) ...
update-initramfs: deferring update (trigger activated)

Processing triggers for initramfs-tools ...
update-initramfs: Generating /boot/initrd.img-2.6.24-zen1-x86
Cannot find /lib/modules/2.6.24-zen1-x86
update-initramfs: failed for /boot/initrd.img-2.6.24-zen1-x86
dpkg: subprocess post-installation script returned error exit status 1

```

And then dumps me back out to the command line.  Any ideas how I can fix this?

--bornagainpenguin

PS: NOTE: I am using an older build of zen.

First, you should upgrade sometime. Second, to fix that you should be able to do a dirty hack by just making the directory. 

```
sudo mkdir /lib/modules/2.6.24-zen1-x86
```

That should fix it. Then, in your package manager make sure that any old pieces of removed past kernels are gone (headers, old images, etc..)

---

### Post by medivh on 2008-04-06
I am using an Asus F3JP (Ati x1700, Intel T7200) and i am a relatively new user. I wanted to install Zen Kernel installed linux-image-2.6.24-zen4_i386_i386.deb and linux-headers-2.6.24-zen4_i386_i386.deb but when i want to start my pc with the new kernel at slash screen nearly when %75 of bar is filled the screen becomes completely black and does not continue. I started with recovery mode and i reached console and typed startx and faced to a completely white screen.

---

### Post by ilikenwf on 2008-04-06
> **medivh said:**
> I am using an Asus F3JP (Ati x1700, Intel T7200) and i am a relatively new user. I wanted to install Zen Kernel installed linux-image-2.6.24-zen4_i386_i386.deb and linux-headers-2.6.24-zen4_i386_i386.deb but when i want to start my pc with the new kernel at slash screen nearly when %75 of bar is filled the screen becomes completely black and does not continue. I started with recovery mode and i reached console and typed startx and faced to a completely white screen.

If you are using nVidia or ATI drivers, you need to set your computer to use a generic linux driver first. Until I figure out how to get nVidia to compile, this is a necessity

Also, when you get to the grub screen, don't select recovery mode, but press "e" on the main zen entry, and then on the next screen use the down arrow to go to the line that has what appears to be a bunch of gibberish on it. At or near the end, remove the word "quiet" and press enter. Then, push b. This will keep the bootscreen from blocking whatever error messages you may be getting, in the event this is not a driver issue.

---

### Post by ilikenwf on 2008-04-07
> **medivh said:**
> It appears to go black screen just after the kernel logger line comes up and i am using fglrx driver. I dont know what you mean by generic linux drivers and how to install them.Sorry about my noobness.

Edit /etc/X11/xorg.conf and change the word "fglrx" to vesa. Either that, or download the installer for your card's driver at ati's website and then follow their instructions to install.

### Post by ilikenwf on 2008-04-15
Disable klogd from an alternative kernel to fix that mess...

As for the broadcom, go download the driver and follow the instructions to the letter on linux wireless (try an older version). The firmware should be dumped into /firmware/b43, not b43-legacy or bcm43xx.

For the modules.dep error you need to make sure you're compiling all the necessary modules you need for your hardware. If something's missing, it isn't pretty.

As for the HDA card, it is highly doubtful that it is fried as a result of software. There are numerous other factors you should check before jumping to the most obvious answer on that. Anyways, I use intel HDA and haven't had a single issue.

Also, I will try to get something out sometime in the near future. I'm playing with Arch right now and have my Kubuntu install backed up as a livecd thanks to Remastersys.

---

As far as zen on arch goes, I have a working compile script, but I'm not sure I see much if any difference between the kernels (and nVidia is a thorn in my side...I broke something with the nVidia installer and I can't use the nVidia driver, even the ARCH one if I remove and reinstall...KDEMod is nice, though.).

---

### Post by ives_13mg on 2008-04-21
Hi. I have an newbie question...
What are the difference in x86_64 and AMD_64? X86_64 is only for Intel?

Another... In /zen/2.6.24-zen4/i386 I didn`t saw an .config file to compile my kernel with our settings... Can I get the .config file that is in /x86_64 folder? 

I`m running Ubuntu 8.04 32-bit...

Bye...

---

### Post by ilikenwf on 2008-04-21
> **ives_13mg said:**
> Hi. I have an newbie question...
What are the difference in x86_64 and AMD_64? X86_64 is only for Intel?

Another... In /zen/2.6.24-zen4/i386 I didn`t saw an .config file to compile my kernel with our settings... Can I get the .config file that is in /x86_64 folder? 

I`m running Ubuntu 8.04 32-bit...

Bye...


The difference is that AMD64 is optimized specifically for AMD processors, and will only run on them. x86_64 will run on any 64 bit, Intel or AMD.

Just use this one, and change the processor settings to suit your system:
[http://www.mattparnell.com/zen/2.6.24-zen4/x86_64/x86_64.config](http://www.mattparnell.com/zen/2.6.24-zen4/x86_64/x86_64.config)

---

Do not fear, though, I still will write a shellscript that will just build the whole thing for you, after you've configured the kernel. That way, you can be as up to date as need be, and perhaps you'll learn something new! 

I will eventually try to find a way to build the debs from gentoo, or cross compile them from my Ubuntu x86 desktop...whatever happens, I'm not going to abandon Zen, it just may be a while before I can get 2.6.25 out.

### Post by yoshic on 2008-05-09
hi! my experience with zen4 i386:

i've got it runnig, i had to disable klogd too and nVidia 3D wiorking, installedlinux-image-2.6.24-zen4_i386_i386, , linux-headers-2.6.24-zen4_i386_i386 and nvidia-kernel-2.6.24-zen4_100.14.19-0ubuntu3+i386_i386, everything downloaded from official site.

i've juts had a problen, nvidia installer complain buecause i didn't have the source, so i downloaded the tarball and put it in /usr/src/sources-zen with its soft link to /usr/src/linux then re-run the  installer and complain againg because it couldn't find version.h file in the sources, so i coimpiled as described in wiki, (without install the deb's generated :? ) then re-run installer again and finally succed the installation... now it runs like a charm:) ... 

hope it helps.

P.S: the nivida package is NVIDIA-Linux-x86-169.12-pkg1.run

### Post by pormogo on 2008-05-17
I think it's worth mentioning that when I compiled my own kernel from that zen source it boots and the kernel log functions just fine, it was something specific to the .deb files that was causing the issue with klogd. 

###Some of this is now fixed :)###
I also noticed that the stock config has ALSA disabled which is where my sound driver happens to reside. On my second recompile this time. I can actually agree now that I have used it for a bit that this kernel is a good deal faster then the generic kernel (however I also built this one with the CORE2 flags set so that could have been making a difference.).

EDIT: Compiling in ALSA and the intel ac97 drivers didn't seem to help anything. Is my sound supported under l-r-m? (##maybe it is, but at this point I was also compiling the wrong driver)

*Audio device: Intel Corporation 82801H (ICH8 Family) HD Audio Controller (rev 02)*

I am still not getting support for my wireless card, is it possible to just throw a symlink somewhere and use the old firmware from my generic kernel on this one? (## yes it was possible, I just had to create a symlink for $kernel-version in /lib/firmware). Below is the error message the network card is giving me. Does the firmware have to be specifically compiled against the kernel headers or something? (##nope all I needed was that symlink =P)

[i][  924.136452] iwl3945: iwlwifi-3945-1.ucode firmware file req failed: Reason -2
[  924.136471] iwl3945: Could not read microcode: -2[/i]

I'm a little confused for how recompiling lrm works. I don't want to recompile all of lrm for all the of the headers that where installed as dependencies when I used apt to install linux-restricted-modules-common. That's going to take a long time and waste a lot of drive space. I know you're supposed to edit the $lrmpath/debian/rules to control how it builds but the description on the wiki is a little vague. Any help would be most appreciated.(##I still don't totally understand how this works)

######

EDIT: Well I finally stopped being lazy and went ahead and REALLY looked into this. I finally figured out there was nothing wrong with the wireless iwl module and the the issue was it finding a firmware ucode. I made my way into /lib/firmware and made a sym link pointing to the generic 2.6.24-16 firmware directory and it worked. 

I also looked over my kernel config again and noticed that I did not compile in support for the Intel HD audio driver and that I installed used some intel AC97 driver for much older boards (or maybe for modem sounds). I have it compiling hopefully one last time with those sound drivers and then I should be good. (## while things now recognize sound I still don't get sound coming out :().

The only single nagging issue seems to be that my bar indicating brighness has disappeared. When I adjust my LCD backlight brightness via fn up or fn down I used to get a little bar letting me know what level of brightness i was at. I am still able to adjust my brightness but using the zen kernel that nifty little bar has disappeared. (##still there)

EDIT2: Well after recompiling again with the intel HD audio drivers I still get no sound out of the Zen kernel. It looks like the module set from the -generic kernel is pretty much the same as in the -zen4 kernel as well (as far as intel HD audio is concerned). 

[i]grep intel utility/lsmod.zen 
snd_hda_intel         342552  3 
snd_pcm                78724  2 snd_hda_intel,snd_pcm_oss
snd_page_alloc         11528  2 snd_hda_intel,snd_pcm
snd_hwdep              10884  1 snd_hda_intel
snd                    56484  15 snd_hda_intel,snd_pcm_oss,snd_mixer_oss,snd_pcm,snd_hwdep,snd_seq_oss,snd_seq,snd_timer,snd_seq_device
intel_agp              27832  1 
agpgart                35788  3 drm,intel_agp
[/i]
And now from the generic kernel lsmod

[i] grep intel utility/lsmod.generic 
snd_hda_intel         353828  6 
snd_pcm                78596  3 snd_hda_intel,snd_pcm_oss
snd_page_alloc         11400  2 snd_hda_intel,snd_pcm
snd_hwdep              10500  1 snd_hda_intel
snd                    56996  21 snd_hda_intel,snd_pcm_oss,snd_mixer_oss,snd_pcm,snd_hwdep,snd_seq_dummy,snd_seq_oss,snd_rawmidi,snd_seq,snd_timer,snd_seq_device
intel_agp              25492  1 
agpgart                34760  3 drm,intel_agp[/i]

the only difference that I can really see is in the "Used by column". I'm pretty confused as to why this isn't working.

### Post by Washer on 2008-05-20
> **pableu said:**
> I think I had to disable klogd to boot the Zen-Kernel under Hardy.

for future reference, the command is ```
sudo rm /etc/rc2.d/*klogd*
```

you could move the links out too instead of deleting them i guess.

edit: ilikenwf says deleting is a bad idea, try renaming as the readme in that folder says

### Post by Washer on 2008-05-20
Sound didn't work for me in hardy either. Well flash sound worked, but mp3s didn't. I figured it's easier to just build a new kernel than try get it working


Edit: well an hour into the compile i noticed the same problem in the generic kernel - flash locks the sound - so I [googled]("http://www.google.com/search?hl=en&client=firefox-a&rls=com.ubuntu%3Aen-US%3Aofficial&q=+site%3Aubuntuforums.org++hardy+mp3+flash+sound&btnG=Search") it & turns out it's a hardy issue. This command seems to have solved it.

```
sudo apt-get purge flashplugin-nonfree gnash gnash-common mozilla-plugin-gnash swfdec-mozilla && sudo apt-get install flashplugin-nonfree libflashsupport
```

---

### Post by ilikenwf on 2008-05-20
> **Washer said:**
> for future reference, the command is ```
sudo rm /etc/rc2.d/*klogd*
```

you could move the links out too instead of deleting them i guess.

NOOO!

You need to rename the SXXklogd files to KXXklogd, that keeps it from starting. It's a bad idea to remove those! (READ THE README OR HELP FILE INSIDE /etc/rc2.d to understand!)
