### Post by ilikenwf on 2008-07-03
I think that it would be best if you all would start compiling this yourselves, if possible. That said, there is a neat script at [http://sharesource.org/project/easypkg/files/95/158/](http://sharesource.org/project/easypkg/files/95/158/) that will allow you to use the Archlinux PKBUILD scripts to build this kernel on your own, with the config settings you choose. You can find a working PKGBUILD at [http://www.mattparnell.com/zen/PKGBUILD/](http://www.mattparnell.com/zen/PKGBUILD/). Just download all the files, and then go through the steps. You need the devel tools, as well as git and qt3/qt4 installed.

To start, chmod +x the easypkg script, run it and use the PKGBUILD file as the input.

I'd suggest using the .config files from my previous releases of Zen as a basis for your setup. I highly suggest the Anticipatory settings, and the preemtive settings, as well as the anticipatory i/o scheduler. If in doubt, see the "matt's config" file in the PKBUILD directory on my server.


In the event easypkg doesn't work, we'll have to all throw in and get it to. If the script asks you if you want to install at the end of the build, say no!

----

I will still write a bash script to do this for you all, eventually. I'm at work right now, so I can't.

---

The new binaries aren't up, because I don't have the 4+ hours it takes every time a new milestone or fix comes about. I'm a college student helping with a political campaign, among other commitments. Furthermore, you need to disable all nvidia video drivers in the kernel, as the nvidiafb in the kernel will break everything. The driver builds just fine if you do this, and patch the installer with the xen hypervisor patch, which is linked to on the wiki page for this kernel, as well as being accessible for the newest drivers via the nvidia forums. [URL="http://www.mattparnell.com/zen/PKGBUILD/nvidia/"]Here, I'll throw you a bone.
[/URL]

> Also reiser4 doesn't work. I have hundreds of GB in a partition & most of it looked corrupted from your kernel. You nearly ruined my day.

I don't write any of the code related to this...you nearly ruined your day, actually. Reiser4 is experimental anyway. You take it all into your own hands when you use a bleeding edge kernel. I'm sorry for the issues; however the devs are working on Reiser4, as well as many other fixes. I will notify you in this thread when it's working.

> Exactly. But image if ubuntu had to keep track of each and every author who ever edited any of the code, AND had to give each author credit. That would be a nightmare.

### Post by durand on 2008-07-15
You probably shouldn't use this if you don't understand a command like chmod. Maybe try it when you know more about linux? You will get all sorts of problems with this kernel and some aren't that easy to fix.

chmod +x buildZen is basically what you run from the terminal: Applications > Accessories > Terminal. 
then use the cd command to go to where you saved the file. For example, if you saved it in your home folder, you don't need to use cd but if you saved it on your desktop, you would type:
```
cd /home/[username]/Desktop
```
or ```
cd ~/Desktop
```
or even ```
cd Desktop/
```

and then you would type:
```
chmod +x buildZen
```. Press Enter after each command.
If you didn't know how to use cd, don't even try the script at the moment!

---

### Post by ilikenwf on 2008-07-16
Good luck, n00b. You'll need it! ;)

As for everyone else, a new branch of the Zen kernel is out, which encorporates the -mm patchset, so it includes everything and the kitchen sink. If you want to use it, the git address is below. You should be able to plug this into my bash script if you use it, by opening it and changing a few things (and saving it under a different name, such as buildZenmm)...first, change the git address, second, change all references to /usr/src/kernel/ to /usr/src/kernel-mm/

Then, it should work. No warranties, as usual, but I've heard zen-mm is possibly faster than the original Zen.

Git address:
git://zen-sources.org/zen/kernel-mm.git

To view the log:
[http://zen-sources.org/cgi-bin/gitweb.cgi?p=kernel-mm.git;a=summary](http://zen-sources.org/cgi-bin/gitweb.cgi?p=kernel-mm.git;a=summary)

dpkg-deb: building package `linux-image-2.6.26-rc9-zen1-20080701' in `../linux-image-2.6.26-rc9-zen1-20080701_2.6.26-rc9-zen1-20080701-10.00.Custom_i386.deb'.

 make-kpkg clean

### Post by ilikenwf on 2008-07-24
> **supertux said:**
> im running the script now. Maybe you can add a check if root is running the script by adding something like: 
if [[ $EUID -ne 0 ]]; then
   echo "This script must be run as root" 1>&2
   exit 1
fi

Gladly...and I'll have it set permissions the first run, now, too.

```

#!/bin/sh

#This script is under the Creative Commons Attribution-Noncommercial-Share Alike 3.0 Unported License. Please attribute it and any part of it you use to Matt Parnell, and #http://www.mattparnell.com/zen/. If you improve or change, or make a fork, please let me know, as well. Contact me at admin@mattparnell.com. To use, chmod +x the script, and then run it by either dropping it into your #/sbin/ dir, or ./buildZen to run it. It pretty well explains everything it's doing. To contact me, or give me #commentary or improvements, see http://www.mattparnell.com/, or email me at admin@mattparnell.com. 

if [[ $EUID -ne 0 ]]; then
echo "This script must be run as root" 1>&2
exit 1
fi

echo -en "
\033[1;32m[INTRODUCTION]
This script will aid you in building the Zen kernel, which you will be building from the git tree. Rerun this script whenever you want to rebuild or update the source tree. 

To continue, type \"y\" if you haven't run this script before, \"b\" if you have run this script before, or \"n\" to exit, and hit enter:\033[1;37m

";

read R;

if [ "$R" = "n" ]; then
exit

elif [ "$R" = "y" ]; then
apt-get update;
apt-get -y install kernel-package libncurses5-dev git git-core bzip2 wget;

chmod -R 777 /usr/src/*

echo "

\033[1;32m[CLONE THE SOURCE TREE]
Now, we must clone the sources via git, using the command \"git clone\". The cloning process takes anywhere from 5 to 60 minutes, sometimes more. Go grab a coffee or surf the web. It's worth the wait. May I suggest browsing mattparnell.com ?\033[1;37m";

cd /usr/src/;
git clone git://zen-sources.org/zen/kernel.git;

echo "

\033[1;32mThe source is now cloned on your local drive.\033[1;37m"

else

echo "

\033[1;32m[UPDATE THE SOURCE TREE]
We don't have to wait from now on. We simply update your copy of the source code by using \"git pull\" from your kernel source directory.\033[1;37m";

cd /usr/src/kernel/;
git pull;

echo "

\033[1;32mYour source is now updated!\033[1;37m";

fi

if [ "$R" = "b" ]; then
echo "

\033[1;32m[CONFIGURE THE KERNEL]
Skipping download of base config, so you can keep your past choices and go from there.\033[1;37m";

else

echo "
\033[1;32m[CONFIGURE THE KERNEL]
Only a few steps left! We need to configure the options for your kernel. First, we need to download a base configuration file that is optimized for your processor.\033[1;37m";

echo "
\033[1;32m
1: 64 bit AMD Processors
2: generic 64 bit support
3: 32 bit processors

Note that you can change the processor type, if you see a more specific option when you configure your kernel, you may choose it instead. It is suggested, especially for 32 bit users, that this be done, as your processor family needs to be selected...keep that in mind!

Enter your choice:\033[1;37m";

read ARC;
cd /usr/src/kernel/;
rm .config;

	if [ "$ARC" = "1" ]; then
	wget http://www.mattparnell.com/zen/prefab/amd64;
	mv amd64 .config;
	elif [ "$ARC" = "2" ]; then
	wget http://www.mattparnell.com/zen/prefab/x86_64;
	mv x86_64 .config;
	else
	wget http://www.mattparnell.com/zen/prefab/x86;
	mv x86 .config;
	fi
fi

echo "

\033[1;32m[CHANGING CONFIGURATION OPTIONS]
From here the options are all up to your discretion. It is suggested that you deselect any drivers, functions, or other options that you know you will not use. If in doubt, disable it. If something is broken or the kernel does not boot, just remove it, re-enable the option, and build. Make sure to take notes your first few tries, and remember to uninstall your old and broken Zen kernels. Always leave a default Ubuntu kernel installed to fall back on! 


To configure your kernel, we need to know what interface you wish to use. 

xconfig:    1
gconfig:    2
menuconfig: 3

When finished, save and close the interface you choose to continue on to the building process.

Choice:\033[1;37m"

read I;
cd /usr/src/kernel/;

if [ "$I" = "1" ]; then
make xconfig;
elif [ "$I" = "2" ]; then
make gconfig;
else
make menuconfig;
fi

echo "

\033[1;32m[BUILD THE KERNEL]
Now that that is all over, we are finally ready to build your kernel. Ubuntu has a script that automates the process, in which it builds your kernel into a nice deb package. You can install that, I hope. All that is left is issuing the command to make that package. This will take some time, and will take all of your computing resources. This is a really good time to walk off for 30 minutes to an hour, and do something else. 

To continue, enter y. Otherwise, enter n to exit:\033[1;37m";

read BD;
cd /usr/src/kernel/;

if [ "$BD" = "y" ]; then
INSTALL_MOD_STRIP=1 CONCURRENCY_LEVEL=2 make-kpkg --initrd kernel_image kernel_headers;
echo "

[FINISHED]
\033[1;32mDone! Exiting. You should be able to figure out how to install your kernel, the normal way with deb packages. 

[SUPPORT]
Read the Zen Kernel entry in the Ubuntu wiki to learn how to install wireless firmware, and setup the TuxOnIce suspend features, among others. To install the nVidia drivers, you will need the nVidia installer, as well as a patch available at http://www.mattparnell.com/zen/PKGBUILD/nvidia/xen.patch.txt .

You may want to see zen-sources.org, as well as the Zen thread on the Gentoo forums, which is linked to at mattparnell.com/zen.html. You can find further support in the Zen thread on Ubuntuforums.\033[1;37m";

else
echo "\033[1;37m"
exit;
fi

```

### Post by BilliShere on 2008-07-28
never mind... it worked.. the mistake was that when you rerun the script after replacing usr/src/ with home/you/ you should actually rerun script  with "y" option instead of "b"

### Post by ilikenwf on 2008-08-18
> **pormogo said:**
> To the best of my knowledge it should be. What particular package am I looking for. I don't see why it wouldn't be alsa is fully functional under my -generic kernel. I don't see why I would need to reinstall any userspace stuff.

I thought alsa was accessed through /proc/asound. PulseAudio is running, and all of my volume controls (alsamixer etc.) appear to be able to access my device. 

I didn't compile in OSS support since it was marked as depreciated (and I don't ever recall compiling OSS into a kernel before).

Don't compile OSS in, but do compile the OSS mixer API that is part of ALSA, as it emulates OSS so that certain programs still can output sound...this may be somethign to report to the Zen-Sources devs...if you ever have a chance, get on irc://irc.freenode.net and join #zen-sources, and tell them what's going on. rmh3093 or waninkoko should be able to help you.

### Post by ilikenwf on 2008-09-07
Now updated, buildZen v2 should work with pretty much any distro, now. It's easiest still with debian based distros, as for all others it checks to see if an automatic build system is in place like portage or abs, and if not, it uses the old fashioned make clean, make, make install, etc...I need people to help me put more checks in for any other build systems to make this really compatible with everything else...oh yeah...and I'll add color again eventually.

```
#!/bin/sh

#This script is opensource under the GPL. Please attribute it and any part of it you use to Matt Parnell, and #http://www.mattparnell.com/zen/. To use, chmod +x the script, and then run it by either dropping it into your #/sbin/ dir, or ./buildZen to run it. It pretty well explains everything it's doing. To contact me, or give me #commentary or improvements, see http://www.mattparnell.com/, or email me at admin@mattparnell.com. 

echo -en "
[INTRODUCTION]
This script will aid you in building the Zen kernel, which you will be building from the git tree. Rerun this script whenever you want to rebuild or update the source tree. 

To continue, type zen to install the regular Zen kernel, zenrt to install the Zen realtime kernel, zenmm to install the Zenmm kernel, or zenps3 to build the Zen for Playstation 3 kernel. Otherwise, enter nothing to exit. Any other input will result in an error. 

";


read repo;

if [ "x${repo}" == "x" ]; then
exit;
fi

echo "[CHECKING FOR BUILD DEPENDENCIES]";

if [[ $(uname -a |grep buntu) != "" || $(uname -a |grep debian) != "" || $(uname -a |grep mint) != "" ]]; then
echo "Installing dependencies";
apt-get update;
apt-get -y install kernel-package libncurses5-dev git bzip2 wget;
fi

if [[ $(which git) == "" ||$(which gcc) == "" || $(which make) == "" || $(which autoconf) == "" || $(which automake) == "" ]]; then 
echo "It appears you do not have gcc, make, autoconf, or automake installed. Please install and rerun this script.";
exit;
fi

echo "It appears you have all build dependencies.


[CLONE THE SOURCE TREE]
Now, we must clone the sources via git, using the command \"git clone\". The cloning process takes anywhere from 5 to 60 minutes, sometimes more. Go grab a coffee or surf the web. It's worth the wait. May I suggest browsing mattparnell.com ?

";

cd /usr/src/;

if [ -d /usr/src/"$repo" ]; then

echo "We just need to update your current source. If any errors happen, and you can't fix them, delete the source folder and try again.";

cd /usr/src/"$repo";
git pull;

echo "Everthing's up to date, or git has timed out.";

else
echo "Cloning "$repo"...";

git clone http://git.zen-sources.org/kernel/"$repo".git;

echo "

The source is now cloned on your local drive."

fi

echo "[CHANGING CONFIGURATION OPTIONS]
From here the options are all up to your discretion. It is suggested that you deselect any drivers, functions, or other options that you know you will not use. If in doubt, disable it. If something is broken or the kernel does not boot, just remove it, re-enable the option, and build. Make sure to take notes your first few tries, and remember to uninstall your old and broken Zen kernels. Always leave a default kernel installed to fall back on! Note that your configuration will be backed up to your home directory.


To configure your kernel, we need to know what interface you wish to use. 

xconfig:    1 (Requires qt)
gconfig:    2 (Requires gtk)
menuconfig: 3 (Requires ncurses)
oldconfig:  4 (Requires bash)

When finished, save and close the interface you choose to continue on to the building process.

Choice: "

read I;
cd /usr/src/"$repo"/;

if [ "$I" = "1" ]; then
make xconfig;
elif [ "$I" = "2" ]; then
make gconfig;
elif [ "$I" = "3" ]; then
make menuconfig;
else
make oldconfig;
fi

cp .config ~/kernel.config;

echo "

[BUILD THE KERNEL]
Now that that is all over, we are finally ready to build your kernel. Ubuntu has a script that automates the process, in which it builds your kernel into a nice deb package. You can install that, I hope. All that is left is issuing the command to make that package. This will take some time, and will take all of your computing resources. This is a really good time to walk off for 30 minutes to an hour, and do something else. 

To continue, enter y. Otherwise, enter n to exit:

";

read BD;
cd /usr/src/"$repo"/;

if [ "$BD" == "n" ]; then
exit;
fi

if [ $(which make-kpkg) != "" ]; then
INSTALL_MOD_STRIP=1 CONCURRENCY_LEVEL=2 make-kpkg --initrd kernel_image kernel_headers modules_image;

echo "Done building, you should have a kernel and headers package to install in /usr/src, as well as a modules package if you opted to put any module source in /usr/src."

elif [ $(which makepkg) != "" ]; then
echo "D'oh. Don't you know there's a PKGBUILD in AUR for this? Go get it, and make sure to move your kernel source tree to the PKGBUILD's appropriate src directory. You may have to edit the git url, as it has changed, and the maintainer is a bit late on updating such things."

else
echo "Doing it the old fashioned way";
make clean;
make;
make bzImage;
make modules;
make modules_install;

echo "Building done. You now need to follow your distro's specific procedures to create a cpio/initrd image, and edit your lilo.conf or /boot/grub/menu.lst file appropriately. See your respective wiki to figure this one out."

echo "
fi

[SUPPORT]
Read the Zen Kernel entry in the Ubuntu wiki to learn how to install wireless firmware, and setup the TuxOnIce suspend features, among others. To install the nVidia drivers, you will need the nVidia installer, as well as a patch available at http://www.mattparnell.com/zen/PKGBUILD/nvidia/xen.patch.txt if it doesn't work.

For live support, feel free to use IRC to connect to irc://irc.freenode.net and join the #zen-sources channel.

You may want to see zen-sources.org, as well as the Zen thread on the Gentoo forums, which is linked to at mattparnell.com/zen.html. You can find further support in the Zen thread on Ubuntuforums.";

echo ""
exit;
```

### Post by ilikenwf on 2008-09-10
You should then still have the packages in /usr/src, so check to see if your new kernel is in there, as everything was built, the bash script just messed up at the end...this should work:

```
#!/bin/sh

#This script is opensource under the GPL. Please attribute it and any part of it you use to Matt Parnell, and #http://www.mattparnell.com/zen/. To use, chmod +x the script, and then run it by either dropping it into your #/sbin/ dir, or ./buildZen to run it. It pretty well explains everything it's doing. To contact me, or give me #commentary or improvements, see http://www.mattparnell.com/, or email me at admin@mattparnell.com. 

echo -en "
[INTRODUCTION]
This script will aid you in building the Zen kernel, which you will be building from the git tree. Rerun this script whenever you want to rebuild or update the source tree. 

To continue, type zen to install the regular Zen kernel, zenrt to install the Zen realtime kernel, zenmm to install the Zenmm kernel, or zenps3 to build the Zen for Playstation 3 kernel. Otherwise, enter nothing to exit. Any other input will result in an error. 

";


read repo;

if [ "x${repo}" == "x" ]; then
exit;
fi

echo "[CHECKING FOR BUILD DEPENDENCIES]";

if [[ $(uname -a |grep buntu) != "" || $(uname -a |grep debian) != "" || $(uname -a |grep mint) != "" ]]; then
echo "Installing dependencies";
apt-get update;
apt-get -y install kernel-package libncurses5-dev git bzip2 wget;
fi

if [[ $(which git) == "" ||$(which gcc) == "" || $(which make) == "" || $(which autoconf) == "" || $(which automake) == "" ]]; then 
echo "It appears you do not have gcc, make, autoconf, or automake installed. Please install and rerun this script.";
exit;
fi

echo "It appears you have all build dependencies.


[CLONE THE SOURCE TREE]
Now, we must clone the sources via git, using the command \"git clone\". The cloning process takes anywhere from 5 to 60 minutes, sometimes more. Go grab a coffee or surf the web. It's worth the wait. May I suggest browsing mattparnell.com ?

";

cd /usr/src/;

if [ -d /usr/src/"$repo" ]; then

echo "We just need to update your current source. If any errors happen, and you can't fix them, delete the source folder and try again.";

cd /usr/src/"$repo";
git pull;

echo "Everthing's up to date, or git has timed out.";

else
echo "Cloning "$repo"...";

git clone http://git.zen-sources.org/kernel/"$repo".git;

echo "

The source is now cloned on your local drive."

fi

echo "[CHANGING CONFIGURATION OPTIONS]
From here the options are all up to your discretion. It is suggested that you deselect any drivers, functions, or other options that you know you will not use. If in doubt, disable it. If something is broken or the kernel does not boot, just remove it, re-enable the option, and build. Make sure to take notes your first few tries, and remember to uninstall your old and broken Zen kernels. Always leave a default kernel installed to fall back on! Note that your configuration will be backed up to your home directory.


To configure your kernel, we need to know what interface you wish to use. 

xconfig:    1 (Requires qt)
gconfig:    2 (Requires gtk)
menuconfig: 3 (Requires ncurses)
oldconfig:  4 (Requires bash)

When finished, save and close the interface you choose to continue on to the building process.

Choice: "

read I;
cd /usr/src/"$repo"/;

if [ "$I" = "1" ]; then
make xconfig;
elif [ "$I" = "2" ]; then
make gconfig;
elif [ "$I" = "3" ]; then
make menuconfig;
else
make oldconfig;
fi

cp .config ~/kernel.config;

echo "

[BUILD THE KERNEL]
Now that that is all over, we are finally ready to build your kernel. Ubuntu has a script that automates the process, in which it builds your kernel into a nice deb package. You can install that, I hope. All that is left is issuing the command to make that package. This will take some time, and will take all of your computing resources. This is a really good time to walk off for 30 minutes to an hour, and do something else. 

To continue, enter y. Otherwise, enter n to exit:

";

read BD;
cd /usr/src/"$repo"/;

if [ "$BD" == "n" ]; then
exit;
fi

if [ $(which make-kpkg) != "" ]; then
INSTALL_MOD_STRIP=1 CONCURRENCY_LEVEL=2 make-kpkg --initrd kernel_image kernel_headers modules_image;

echo "Done building, you should have a kernel and headers package to install in /usr/src, as well as a modules package if you opted to put any module source in /usr/src."

elif [ $(which makepkg) != "" ]; then
echo "D'oh. Don't you know there's a PKGBUILD in AUR for this? Go get it, and make sure to move your kernel source tree to the PKGBUILD's appropriate src directory. You may have to edit the git url, as it has changed, and the maintainer is a bit late on updating such things."

else
echo "Doing it the old fashioned way";
make clean;
make;
make bzImage;
make modules;
make modules_install;
fi

echo "Building done. You now need to follow your distro's specific procedures to create a cpio/initrd image, and edit your lilo.conf or /boot/grub/menu.lst file appropriately. See your respective wiki to figure this one out.


[SUPPORT]
Read the Zen Kernel entry in the Ubuntu wiki to learn how to install wireless firmware, and setup the TuxOnIce suspend features, among others. To install the nVidia drivers, you will need the nVidia installer, as well as a patch available at http://www.mattparnell.com/zen/PKGBUILD/nvidia/xen.patch.txt if it doesn't work.

For live support, feel free to use IRC to connect to irc://irc.freenode.net and join the #zen-sources channel.

You may want to see zen-sources.org, as well as the Zen thread on the Gentoo forums, which is linked to at mattparnell.com/zen.html. You can find further support in the Zen thread on Ubuntuforums.";

exit;
```

### Post by soundcheck on 2008-11-24
Hi folks.

I just installed 2.6.28-rc6-zen1. 
It worked pretty smooth. 
(It is not the first ZEN kernel I installed. I do the installation manually.)  

Even without fglrx the system responds extremely fast now. ( I am running
the ZEN "gaming" option and CFS scheduler)

One thing I would like to discuss. 

"fglrx dkms auto-install"

With Intrepid Ubuntu introduced or fixed a dkms-autoinstall procedure for fglrx to be able
to boot more then one Ubuntu-kernel with fglrx on one system.
While booting this or that kernel fglrx will be newly installed.

Now: The ZEN kernel challenge would be to 

a. get fglrx installed properly first of all and 
b. even auto-installed during boot


Do you guys have any idea how to tackle this issue?  
I regard this as one of the major obstacles associated to ZEN and Ubuntu.

The key is the  dkms autoinstall script  /etc/init.d/dkms_autoinstaller

and the /var/lib/dkms/ directory, where the modules are stored.


The current error message /var/log/dkms_autoinstaller is

fglrx (8.552): Installing module.
......(bad exit status: 7)
Build failed.  Installation skipped.

If you look in the script  it seems that it fails because,
the kernel structure for the ZEN kernel is not present under /var/lib/dkms


I'd appreciate if somebody would join this discussion. I'll dig further into it.
 

Off topic proposal to ilikenwf: It might be a good idea to open up a new thread for the 2.6.28-zen-kernel. 
 

THX & Cheers

---

### Post by soundcheck on 2008-11-24
Hi.

Next finding:

On a standard ZEN-kernel fglrx.ko won't compile 
(pretty old but still valid problem as it seems)


/usr/src/linux/kernel/rcupreempt.c

AS-IS:

EXPORT_SYMBOL_GPL(__rcu_read_lock)
EXPORT_SYMBOL_GPL(__rcu_read_unlock)

TO-BE

EXPORT_SYMBOL(__rcu_read_lock)
EXPORT_SYMBOL(__rcu_read_unlock)



I am wondering why there is still no patch for that?

Anyhow. I'll keep digging.

Cheers

display: :0.0  screen: 0
OpenGL vendor string: ATI Technologies Inc.
OpenGL renderer string: ATI MOBILITY FireGL V5200
OpenGL version string: 2.1.8201 FireGL Release

soundcheck@think:~$ uname -a
Linux think1 2.6.28-rc6-zen1 #1 PREEMPT Mon Nov 24 15:13:18 CET 2008 i686 GNU/Linux

### Post by ilikenwf on 2008-11-25
"Owner?" It's opensource...there's no such thing. I don't mind..I appreciate it, in fact. 

You all may want to note that the Zen official repo is down at the moment. For the time being, use [http://repo.or.cz/w/linux-2.6/zen-sources.git](http://repo.or.cz/w/linux-2.6/zen-sources.git) (rather, go there and get the git url).

Currently, only the vanilla/regular Zen is available.

Furthermore, the concurrency thing is a matter of choice, and modules_image builds any modules that may be in /usr/src/, if you do things the ubuntu way.


YOU DON'T NEED THE HYPERVISOR PATCH FOR nVidia anymore...I'll change that in the wiki.

---

### Post by soundcheck on 2008-11-27
You got pretty far already! :D Great.

Your /usr/src has bad permissions. Happened to me before.

You need to change it to 755 or 775 

$ sudo chmod 775 /usr /usr/src

and than compile again.

run a sudo make-kpkg clean first

you'll find the .debs in /usr/src afterwards

Good luck.

---

### Post by The_Rebel52 on 2009-02-02
Do zen-kernels work with DKMS?

I can seem to get lirc-modules-source to compile with DKMS (it won't compile with automake either)

---

### Post by soundcheck on 2009-02-03
> **The_Rebel52 said:**
> Do zen-kernels work with DKMS?

I can seem to get lirc-modules-source to compile with DKMS (it won't compile with automake either)

DKMS is beyond the scope of ZEN. Ubuntu is using it.
E.g. FGLRX needs to be patched (GPL) to get it compiled at all. Then DKMS needs to be setup to install fglrx during boot. 
Recently Ubuntu  introduced an autoinstallation routine to get fglrx installed during boot. This even works for a ZEN-kernel.

So I guess it is a two step apporach. 

You might want to check with the guys at zen-sources.org. There are some Ubuntu guys around. 

Cheers

---
